  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

  <span id="freeText13562418004351733006" style="display:none"><p>After years of great sacrifice and deep personal tragedy, Florentyna Kane’s has finally become the first woman president in America. But on the very day that she is sworn into office, powerful forces are already in motion to take her life.<b></b></p><p>The FBI investigates thousands of false threats every year. This time, a reliable source has tipped them off about an assassination attempt. One hour later, the informant and all but one of the investigating agents are dead. The lone survivor: FBI Special Agent Mark Andrews. Now, only he knows when the killers will strike. But how can he alone unravel a ruthless conspiracy—in less than one week? The race to save the first woman president begins <i>now…</i></p></span>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3501814372?book_show_action=true">Aug 18, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/49365462-w?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/49365462-w?shelf=archer">archer</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3501814372" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1618369664941187632">Archer wrote two versions of this book.In the first one,Ted Kennedy was the fictional president against whom an assassination plot was being hatched. <br/><br/>Later,Archer wrote the second version.In this one,Florentyna Kane becomes the first female president of the US and now she is the target of the assassins.<br/><br/>It is an action packed thriller in which the president herself,makes very brief appearances.<br/><br/>The story centres around FBI agent,Mark Andrews. The FBI finds an injured man who claims to have heard a</span>
  <span id="freeText1618369664941187632" style="display:none">Archer wrote two versions of this book.In the first one,Ted Kennedy was the fictional president against whom an assassination plot was being hatched. <br /><br />Later,Archer wrote the second version.In this one,Florentyna Kane becomes the first female president of the US and now she is the target of the assassins.<br /><br />It is an action packed thriller in which the president herself,makes very brief appearances.<br /><br />The story centres around FBI agent,Mark Andrews. The FBI finds an injured man who claims to have heard about an assassination plot.But very soon,the man is dead and so are two FBI agents.<br /><br />The president wants to introduce a gun control bill in the US,and someone dislikes the idea enough to want to kill her.There are seven days in which to foil the plot.<br /><br />This is a page turner with non-stop action.<br />Gun related violence continues unabated in the US and gun control laws are not likely to see the light of day,despite all the massacres that have taken place.<br /><br />The book can be read as a standalone.It is not exactly Kane and Abel # 3.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1618369664941187632" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer7239444909935831822">I came across this book recently but I forgot it was first published in 1977. It is an exciting political thriller.....a real page turner.   <span id="freeText7239444909935831822" style="display:none">I came across this book recently but I forgot it was first published in 1977. It is an exciting political thriller.....a real page turner. And yet the scenario could fall right into the politics of 2020 ! The first woman President , Florentyna Kane is attempting to get passed, an important gun control law . Little does she know that a Senator and some criminals will stop at nothing to get the law to fail......including the assassination of the President.<br /> This is a non-stop thriller which could easily fall into the scenario of the present political climate......except this administration would let anyone who wants to own a gun have access to one. The FBI is in the middle of the case and will do anything to stop the assassination. <br />Enjoy ! One of the cute things Archer brings to this book is that some of the people are real people ou know from the world of politics !</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarah" href="/user/show/387635-sarah">Sarah</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer128767200" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10926787938446662514">A rookie agent has to stop the assassination of the President. So this book wasn't bad so much as ridiculous. It was written a long time ago about the future 43rd president, then updated and published again after there had been a real 43rd president. I really think I might have liked it had I read it in 1977 or something. But it was just surreal, and not in a good way, to read someone's vision of the 2000s. He got to first female president, but didn't quite think of the internet. So the hero is </span>
  <span id="freeText10926787938446662514" style="display:none">A rookie agent has to stop the assassination of the President. So this book wasn't bad so much as ridiculous. It was written a long time ago about the future 43rd president, then updated and published again after there had been a real 43rd president. I really think I might have liked it had I read it in 1977 or something. But it was just surreal, and not in a good way, to read someone's vision of the 2000s. He got to first female president, but didn't quite think of the internet. So the hero is just doing all his research at the library with a stack of quarters from a pay phone. On an unrelated note, even if the technology had been updated, I just really got angry at the hero's passionate love for the heroine aka a possible accomplice of the assassin. The deal was that they met and he just fell too head over heels and believed so much in love and his right to love that he couldn't stay away from her for the 6 days to the presumptive assassination. I wonder if it's annoying to me because it really is annoying or because in the post-2001 world nothing like that seems believable (just like pay phones).</span>
  <a data-text-id="10926787938446662514" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2492137410" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2492137410" />
    <a title="Pamela" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17527831-pamela"><img alt="Pamela" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1504263912p2/17527831.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2492137410?book_show_action=true">Aug 17, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Pamela" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Pamela" href="/user/show/17527831-pamela">Pamela</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2492137410" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9202497342207725728">Entertaining and suspenseful! However, it is not a serious political thriller. There are too many implausible events and unanswered questions. There is excitement and razor tension from the first page, but it loses that cutting edge to the point that the climax is anti-climactic. The denouement is flat as well. The characters are very well developed and it is disappointing that this marks the ending of a great series.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/120417615?book_show_action=true">Sep 06, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Benjamin Thomas" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Benjamin Thomas" href="/user/show/4209082-benjamin-thomas">Benjamin Thomas</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780312933517" href="/book/show/4890696-shall-we-tell-the-president">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4209082-benjamin-thomas?shelf=thriller-political">thriller-political</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer120417615" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11649026458826904932">This started out as Jeffrey Archer's second published novel, quite a few years ago, but has now been updated for more current politics. Try to find the original version, because it is vintage early Archer. In the original version, the novel begins just after Ed Kennedy is sworn in as president after Jimmy Carter. It was a rough time in American history, and Archer weaves the mood of the times into the story. The plot revolves around a junior FBI agent's investigation into an assassination attemp</span>
  <span id="freeText11649026458826904932" style="display:none">This started out as Jeffrey Archer's second published novel, quite a few years ago, but has now been updated for more current politics. Try to find the original version, because it is vintage early Archer. In the original version, the novel begins just after Ed Kennedy is sworn in as president after Jimmy Carter. It was a rough time in American history, and Archer weaves the mood of the times into the story. The plot revolves around a junior FBI agent's investigation into an assassination attempt against the new president. He juggles a new relationship with the daughter of a senator who just happens to be a prime suspect in the conspiracy. Archer demonstrates his US political expertise here, despite being an Englishman. This novel goes behind the scenes of Washington DC, though not nearly to the extent his later novel, First Among Equals, does in London's Parliament. My only real complaint with the novel is its lack of major plot twists which I've come to expect from Archer's works. Pretty straight forward story. If you enjoy Archer's works, try to locate a copy of this one too. </span>
  <a data-text-id="11649026458826904932" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText9795713381028842123" style="display:none">I bought this book on my kindle before I read the reviews on it. From what I now understand it was changed and updated from the original version of the hardback that was published in the 1970's. It has been a very long time since I read the first two books in this series "Kane and Abel" and "The Prodigal Daughter" but I was expecting this book to be more about the main character "the president" then it was.   <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2036964797?book_show_action=true">Jul 04, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jim C" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jim C" href="/user/show/10296231-jim-c">Jim C</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/11477585-shall-we-tell-the-president">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2036964797" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17335212819628669537">This is the final book of a trilogy. It can be read as a stand alone. In this one, there is a plan to kill the president because she supports a gun control bill. The FBI race to discover who is behind the conspiracy to kill the president.<br/><br/>This was a lousy way to finish this trilogy. The first two books were excellent. The only positive I can take away from this novel is it tackling the issue of gun control. The author accomplished this without preaching. He expressed both sides concerns and why i</span>
  <span id="freeText17335212819628669537" style="display:none">This is the final book of a trilogy. It can be read as a stand alone. In this one, there is a plan to kill the president because she supports a gun control bill. The FBI race to discover who is behind the conspiracy to kill the president.<br /><br />This was a lousy way to finish this trilogy. The first two books were excellent. The only positive I can take away from this novel is it tackling the issue of gun control. The author accomplished this without preaching. He expressed both sides concerns and why it is an issue today. I especially liked this since this was written many years ago. Besides that this book did not have anything going for it. First of all, it was not a "Kane &amp; Abel" novel. The character used from those books was used as a gimmick attempting to tie in this book with the others. Secondly, the investigation had its flaws. It was boring and the turns were a stretch with some of its plot holes. There was one time I actually groaned out loud.<br /><br />This book had the right idea but it never executed them to be satisfactory. I liked the issue but it was not enough to deem this a worthy read. It was false advertising and I recommend stopping after the second book of this trilogy.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17335212819628669537" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer1669816037906971951">The first book in this trilogy — Kane & Abel — was about the story of two diverse boys from their birth to mid-age and how different events led them to success as well as hatred for each other. It was, as I've written in the review, one of the best books I've ever read, and I gave it 5 stars.<br/><br/>The second — The Prodigal Daughter — was about the rise of Abel's daughter first as a student, then a businesswoman and finally as a politician. I gave it 4 stars.<br/><br/>Unfortunately, this book turned out to be a </span>
  <span id="freeText1669816037906971951" style="display:none">The first book in this trilogy — Kane &amp; Abel — was about the story of two diverse boys from their birth to mid-age and how different events led them to success as well as hatred for each other. It was, as I've written in the review, one of the best books I've ever read, and I gave it 5 stars.<br /><br />The second — The Prodigal Daughter — was about the rise of Abel's daughter first as a student, then a businesswoman and finally as a politician. I gave it 4 stars.<br /><br />Unfortunately, this book turned out to be a FBI suspense thriller and I've read much better FBI/CIA thrillers. Also, there are just too many inconsistencies, especially when it refers to events in The Prodigal Daughter. There are also glaring errors: such as the Secret Service being called Secret Police.</span>

  <span id="freeText10482587760889418266" style="display:none">Goodreads Book Blurb:<br><br>After years of great sacrifice and deep personal tragedy, Florentyna Kane’s has finally become the first woman president in America. But on the very day that she is sworn into office, powerful forces are already in motion to take her life.<br><br>The FBI investigates thousands of false threats every year. This time, a reliable source has tipped them off about an assassination attempt. One hour later, the informant and all but one of the investigating agents are dead. The lone survivor: FBI Special Agent Mark Andrews. Now, only he knows when the killers will strike. But how can he alone unravel a ruthless conspiracy—in less than one week? The race to save the first woman president begins now…<br><br>4 STARS – Would Highly Recommend To Others<br><br>I love Jeffrey Archer’s books and have read several of them. This was written decades ago and can still compete with the more sophisticated books of the present.<br><br>Marc Andrews is on his own to find out who wants the president dead. Time is running out as he tries to eliminate the suspects.The suspense builds as the danger closes in on him.<br><br>For conspiracy theorists, this is a book you will want to read. I always figure, it is someone close to you who poses the biggest threat, because you believe and trust them. They can look you in the eye as they lie and plot against you. Such is the case here. Be sure to look to your right, left, front and back as you turn the pages. You never know where the strike will come from.<br><br>I still think of the Kennedy assassination and whether or not there was a government conspiracy that brought him down. Why would that be so impossible to believe? Our government is no less greedy and corrupt than any third world country. How far would someone go to achieve their goal? Look around at present day events and you may find your answer.<br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/78989.Shall_We_Tell_the_President___Kane___Abel___3_" title="Shall We Tell the President? (Kane &amp; Abel, #3) by Jeffrey Archer" rel="nofollow noopener">

</a><br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4820.Jeffrey_Archer" title="Jeffrey Archer" rel="nofollow noopener">Jeffrey Archer</a></span>

  <span id="freeText16361342760245354472" style="display:none">(2.5 / 5)<br /><br />I had read this book about 7 or 8 years back when I was in school, and I was so thrilled! I thought that it was an underrated roller coaster. But after reading it again now I realize how wrong I was! It isn't a particularly bad book, but it has a lot of plot holes, in addition to being very unrealistic. The protagonist works like a newbie, not like a Special Agent of the Federal Bureau of Investigation. The criminals are hardly "professional" as oft mentioned in the book. And after having recently read the amazing <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/36064.American_Tabloid__Underworld_USA___1_" title="American Tabloid (Underworld USA, #1) by James Ellroy" rel="nofollow noopener">American Tabloid</a> by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2887.James_Ellroy" title="James Ellroy" rel="nofollow noopener">James Ellroy</a>, Shall We Tell the President pales in comparison.<br /><br />And I would also like to rant against the new edition that continues the story from The Prodigal Daughter. WHY, ARCHER, WHY? I prefer the one that did not have Kane as the President. It definitely made more sense and her presence in this book looks clearly forced.</span>

  <span id="freeText3614447752852042827" style="display:none">They say most criminals are caught because of one, decisive mistake. With that in mind, I wonder how many assassination plots are discussed in clear and certain terms casually over lunch within earshot of the wait staff and other patrons. Not many? Yeah, I didn't think so either.<br /><br />Also, considering the entire purpose of the rubout was to stall a bill on gun control (one which specifically limits criminal access to firearms), was having a criminal use an illegal firearm on the POTUS really the best strategy? Something tells me that would only hasten such a bill. Aye yai yai.<br /><br />For what it's worth, the pacing is pretty good and Archer at least keeps you engaged to the end. But that hardly makes up for the nonsensical plot.<br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_2380797253" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2380797253" />
    <a title="Rohit Sharma" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/52092570-rohit-sharma"><img alt="Rohit Sharma" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1483636783p2/52092570.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2380797253?book_show_action=true">Aug 22, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rohit Sharma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rohit Sharma" href="/user/show/52092570-rohit-sharma">Rohit Sharma</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2380797253" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12195581792260285570">A couple of months back I re-read the iconic "Kane and Abel" but unfortunately this time around it didn't work for me. That typical Jeffrey Archer magic was missing, I just couldn't believe myself that I wasn't able to like it that much as I expected it to be. So I went ahead and read its sequel with very high hopes of liking it, and guess what, I was right :). The sequel "The Prodigal Daughter" was fantastic and with very high hopes I picked up the last of the trilogy last week to check if it w</span>
  <span id="freeText12195581792260285570" style="display:none">A couple of months back I re-read the iconic "Kane and Abel" but unfortunately this time around it didn't work for me. That typical Jeffrey Archer magic was missing, I just couldn't believe myself that I wasn't able to like it that much as I expected it to be. So I went ahead and read its sequel with very high hopes of liking it, and guess what, I was right :). The sequel "The Prodigal Daughter" was fantastic and with very high hopes I picked up the last of the trilogy last week to check if it will keep the momentum going. And let me tell you at the very start, the third book of the trilogy is technically the best book of the lot, it was simply superb and I must say Uncle Archer was totally back with all the action, on top of that a terrific love story too as an added bonus in this one. Although the character of Florentyna Kane took a backseat and makes way for the FBI agent(s) who just keeps asking his boss "Shall We Tell the President?". What secret they keep from the President or do they actually get to tell her, is something I read the book for and it did keep me glued to the very end in the most mesmerizing way. My trust on Archer Uncle is back with a bang and I am so much looking forward to read so much more from him. May be I will get all his earlier works and read them as and when I can :). He is one of my all time favorite writers for sure. <br /><br />At the end of the second book, Florentyna is made the President of United States. At least in fiction, Archer gives Americans their first woman President and the first thing she wants to do is to control the fire arms. How kool is that :) again, this can be done only in fiction, and no ways in real life. As she gets closer to pass the bill for controlling the fire arms and their sale in USA, there are people who want to remove her from the power. The only way to do it is to kill her, who is behind the conspiracy and how a rookie FBI agent comes across the information and takes it ahead with the agency makes up for a perfectly thrilling Cat and Mouse chase game. The three most important characters of the story are the agent, his accidental girl friend and the terrific Director of FBI, whose first name is never disclosed in the whole story as that carries a cash prize of $3516, to anyone who gets it first. I actually had to keep a keen eye to see if I could actually find the name mentioned somewhere. Why that odd figure? You've got to read the book to find that out. It was such a thrilling story with so much going on in typical American way, on top of that Archer leaves no stone upturned in making it a superb love story as well. How he does that in so much style is something which always impresses me big time and makes me a fan of the man. Life inside the Capitol building in DC as well as inside the FBI headquarters is captured in such a beautiful yet hooking way that it kept me glued to the book throughout. <br /><br />Have you read the Kane and Abel trilogy? Which one is your favorite from the three? Mine is definitely "Shall We Tell the President" without any doubts. Even as an Individual book, it will be a wonderful read as not much connection with the previous two parts but just a handful of characters, who again get not so much attention in this one. </span>
  <a data-text-id="12195581792260285570" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3199288815" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3199288815" />
    <a title="Anne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/56446521-anne"><img alt="Anne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1465042652p2/56446521.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3199288815?book_show_action=true">Jun 30, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anne" href="/user/show/56446521-anne">Anne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780006478676" href="/book/show/830520.Shall_We_Tell_The_President_">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3199288815" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17368555555777398576">To be honest I wasn't sure if this was a 2 or 3 star book but after running it through CAWPILE it was a 2 star. This wasn't necessarily a terrible book, the plot was...okay ish (like basically your standard action movie but in book form) - but there is a lot of weird internal monologuing that is often bordering on the homophobic, racist, and sexist/predatory. Its fine if a character has these internal beliefs, but they are never challenged and they are dropped so casually throughout the second h</span>
  <span id="freeText17368555555777398576" style="display:none">To be honest I wasn't sure if this was a 2 or 3 star book but after running it through CAWPILE it was a 2 star. This wasn't necessarily a terrible book, the plot was...okay ish (like basically your standard action movie but in book form) - but there is a lot of weird internal monologuing that is often bordering on the homophobic, racist, and sexist/predatory. Its fine if a character has these internal beliefs, but they are never challenged and they are dropped so casually throughout the second half of the book, it doesn't make sense. This is also another thing that bothers me, the first and second halves of the books seem to be written in 2 extremely different styles, to the point where I even wonder if Archer spend like 9 months writing the first half and woke up one day and realized "fuck I need to deliver this book tomorrow"and downed 2 cans of Energy drinks and typed the rest out in 12 hours, and because he needed to get more words he decided "okay I'm randomly going to make Mark really really concerned about being too black or looking gay or behave like a predator" but not even only that - he does all of this in Bullet point sentences that feels like the author just didn't have enough time to write out all the sentences and he just decided to remove the bullet points and just stick all the sentences back to back with full stops. <br /><br />Another thing I want to point out is that this book is nothing at all like the first two books in the series. The first two books are two really interesting strategic novels, the first is more leaning towards personal history and business and it follows 2 characters who come from very different backgrounds, the second follows one of their daughters as she tries to become the first female president of the united states. These books were both really nuanced and brought interesting discussions to the table about a wide array of things - this book did none of that, its like the opposite of that. Its short and uninteresting and lacks everything that made the previous books interesting. To be honest I might not have disliked this book so much if I hadn't read it with the expectation that it was a sequel to two books that I both enjoyed quite a bit, they weren't never favorites but there was a standard I was used to. </span>
  <a data-text-id="17368555555777398576" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1512625696" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1512625696" />
    <a title="Hernie YR" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12846634-hernie-yr"><img alt="Hernie YR" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1433480897p2/12846634.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1512625696?book_show_action=true">Feb 08, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hernie YR" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hernie YR" href="/user/show/12846634-hernie-yr">Hernie YR</a>
      </span>

          added it


          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780330418966" href="/book/show/79012.Shall_We_Tell_the_President_">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12846634-hernie-yr?shelf=mine-oh-mine">mine-oh-mine</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1512625696" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14086722117471586576">I liked it. Though it was a supposed #3 of the series, it was written before Kane & Abel. I liked how he recycled his characters. I liked the fact that it was a part of a series and yet, not a conclusion. I liked that each book has its own focus. <br/><br/>Jeffrey Archer has found his way into my list of favourite authors.</span>
  <span id="freeText14086722117471586576" style="display:none">I liked it. Though it was a supposed #3 of the series, it was written before Kane &amp; Abel. I liked how he recycled his characters. I liked the fact that it was a part of a series and yet, not a conclusion. I liked that each book has its own focus. <br /><br />Jeffrey Archer has found his way into my list of favourite authors.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14086722117471586576" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3187696709" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Sumit Khanna" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10375541-sumit-khanna"><img alt="Sumit Khanna" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598290556p2/10375541.jpg" /></a>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2221933185" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2221933185" />
    <a title="Boni Aditya" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/21136796-boni-aditya"><img alt="Boni Aditya" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1571443815p2/21136796.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2221933185?book_show_action=true">Dec 22, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Boni Aditya" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Boni Aditya" href="/user/show/21136796-boni-aditya">Boni Aditya</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21136796-boni-aditya?shelf=novels-fiction">novels-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2221933185" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16863013126004091378">This book is not extra ordinary! Please understand that it barely keeps the suspense. It was extremely obvious how the plot would turn out to be! The author played with romancing the villains daughter theme for a bit then with FBI trickery for some time and then more about the political drama. In the end like always the president is saved, the sniper is caught and the bill is passed! <br/><br/>The book is predictable, we know what is going to happen next, for example, the first time when I heard of a SIMO</span>
  <span id="freeText16863013126004091378" style="display:none">This book is not extra ordinary! Please understand that it barely keeps the suspense. It was extremely obvious how the plot would turn out to be! The author played with romancing the villains daughter theme for a bit then with FBI trickery for some time and then more about the political drama. In the end like always the president is saved, the sniper is caught and the bill is passed! <br /><br />The book is predictable, we know what is going to happen next, for example, the first time when I heard of a SIMON who drives around the Hero Andrews car, it is quite evident that he is going to die. The scene where the bishop comes to the widow, or when the bishop comes into the hospital, is a scene all too well used in hollywood, when the most revered person slits the throats and commits the murders - so that nobody suspects anything. <br /><br />May be I have watched too many Hollywood films that I have become too accustomed to such plots or may be the plot is merely average. In either case, it is merely a waste of some time.<br /><br />The Bad:<br />The parts that irked me the most were when he recites the daily time table of Mark, Get up the bed - brush - half past seven - get down the car - .... That, was the worst part of the book. I should say. The predictability ruined any chance of surprise and the plot had so many names of the senators and so much rubbish all in all. The lack of focus on a character as an arch rival or a staunch enemy is piercing.<br /><br />The Good: The flow of the topic, in a structured fashion and the ability of the author to make the text run in a smooth fashion would keep the reader engaged, though not super energetic. But it is simple and would keep running. To follow up the text is easy, the writing style is good. It does not require literary expertise to understand what he is saying. The characters all have their role. Nobody is downplayed.<br /><br />The UGLY: This is not the mistake of the author. He was living in a time when there were no mobile phones, no internet and definitely no databases. Many chapters were wasted, by Mark Andrews searching for information, now that information can be obtained while I rest on my bed. Unfortunately we see the author run around for people, for transcripts for addresses. I can't find fault with the author for having wasted his time on trite details. The book must get a remake with a better plot and stronger villain. The villain is just so "easy come - easy go" He does not seem to have a PLAN B! PLAN B is to kill himself? What kind of a plan is that?<br /><br />RETROSPECTION:<br /><br />I now understand why people read current books. "Assassination of a Leader" is a concept that is as old as politics itself. Though the concept is the same, reading the assassination attempt of 1980's seems like child's play compared to the assassination attempts of 2010 - 2020; Assassins these days go the full nine yards and have unique ways of killing people by using seemingly simple objects like poisoned pins or brain altering viruses. This assassination seems like kids bashing each other in the parking lot. I always had this question "Hundreds of thousands of books have already been written by millions of authors since books were first printed, is there anything new that I can write or any author could write? Anything that is written today would be similar to what has already been written" I think this book answers that question! (SIMILAR != SAME) "The Devil is in the Details" Though the concept is the same "KILL THE PRESIDENT" the details are extremely different! What Mark Andrews did in 1980's vs what he would have done or what FBI would have done now is worlds apart. Reading old novels would have made sense if it was 1600s or 1700s where the world would have changed at snails pace. Now the world started changing much more rapidly. So the novels become outdated i.e. the details in the novels become outdated with each passing year. So effectively you don't have to come up with a new concept each time you want to write a novel. You can merely choose an existing concept and use new colors, since with each passing year we seem to invent millions of new shades of colors. You can just take and old painting and make it finer and more finer. Thus a simple Zombie Genre can now be colored in thousand finer ways or more. People might say it is just another Zombie novel, but wait, this a zombie novel of 2017 not the Zombie novel of 1960s. This is the "I am Legend" not the "Last Man on Earth" - THERE IS A DIFFERENCE - albeit a subtle one but nonetheless striking! It is the difference between keeping the reader interested and raising apathy in the reader. He is just shuffling change and calling from a pay phone, that is just so boring! Now-a-days we rarely see any pay phones!</span>
  <a data-text-id="16863013126004091378" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('tIzLVDrvrvbAdgUsGr8l8rDYNjfQYzUxxre7+vxB+b1Ty9Yajf9+jEClevv1p/jtduq1t3RWs86KAJXRXNL70A==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('AeBs7JnFotnvZDgD3tKIdQRq6je16wrc6fxKTYo6OFXmp3GiLtVyo2+3R9QxylVqwlhptxHejCOlS2RmKqk6OA==')})
  }

<span id="freeTextContainer10637011949996451337">Jeffrey Howard Archer, Baron Archer of Weston-super-Mare (born 15 April 1940) is an English author and former politician.<br/><br/>He was a Member of Parliament and deputy chairman of the Conservative Party, and became a life peer in 1992. His political career, having suffered several controversies, ended after a conviction for perverting the course of justice and his subsequent imprisonment. He is married </span>
  <span id="freeText10637011949996451337" style="display:none">Jeffrey Howard Archer, Baron Archer of Weston-super-Mare (born 15 April 1940) is an English author and former politician.<br /><br />He was a Member of Parliament and deputy chairman of the Conservative Party, and became a life peer in 1992. His political career, having suffered several controversies, ended after a conviction for perverting the course of justice and his subsequent imprisonment. He is married to Mary Archer, a scientist specialising in solar power. Outside politics, he is a novelist, playwright and short story writer.<br /><br /><a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jeffrey_Archer" rel="nofollow noopener">Wikipedia link</a><br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://us.macmillan.com/author/jeffreyarcher">http://us.macmillan.com/author/jeffre...</a></span>
